مجلس (majlis): The session or gathering in which the husband delegates the choice; actions after leaving the session are not considered connected.

Repeating 'Ikhari' and Triple Divorce: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of repeating 'Ikhari' on triple divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on triple divorce when the husband repeats 'Ikhari' and evaluate the proofs of each side.

Core Idea
When 'Ikhari' is repeated, some Hanafis rule triple divorce without intention; others require intent for the triple to take effect.

The word 'Ikhari' (choose) is a classic tool for delegation of divorce. If the husband says it two or three times and the wife chooses one instance, does triple divorce automatically occur? This question sparks an intra-Hanafi dispute. In this lesson, we unpack the arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether triple divorce occurs when the husband repeats 'Ikhari' multiple times and the wife selects one of the instances, without the husband intending triple divorce.
The key is the legal effect of repetition without explicit intent.
2
State the first Hanafi position
The author (following al-Hidayah, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and al-Atabi) holds that triple divorce occurs without any need for intention. The repetition itself indicates a desire for divorce.
This view relies on the principle that multiplicity pertains to divorce (which is limited to three) and not to other matters.
3
State the second Hanafi position
Qadi Khan and Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi require intention for triple divorce to occur. Repetition is ambiguous and could refer to choosing in property or dwelling, so intention must be manifest.
They analogize to the case of repeating 'I'tadi' (observe iddah), which does not automatically imply divorce.
4
Analyze the counter-arguments
The first group responds that what is limited to three is divorce, not other choices. Also, if the husband says 'Ikhari' only twice, divorce occurs even without intention, supporting their view.
The second group's position is preferred in Fath al-Qadir, indicating a tarjih toward requiring intention.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If intention is required, the husband can deny triple divorce and only one divorce (the delegated one) occurs. If not required, triple divorce is effective regardless of inner intent.
This affects the validity of the marriage and further remarriage options.

قوله: (ولو قال لها اختاري اختاري فقالت اخترت الأولى أو الوسطى أو الأخيرة وقع الثلاث بلا نية لأن في لفظه ما يدل على إرادة الطلاق وهو التعدد وهو إنما يتعلق بالطلاق لا باختيار الزوج، وقد اختلف المشايخ في الوقوع به قضاء بدون النية مع الاتفاق على أنه لا يقع في نفس الأمر بالنية، فذهب المصنف تبعاً لصاحب الهداية والصدر الشهيد والعتابي إلى عدم اشتراطها لما ذكرنا، وذهب قاضيخان وأبو المعين النسفي إلى اشتراطها، ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن تكرار أمره بالاختيار لا يصير ظاهراً في الطلاق لجواز أن يريد اختاري في المال واختاري في المسكن ونحوه. وهو كاعتدي إذا كرره. وقد يجاب عنه بأن المحصور بالثلاث هو الطلاق لا أمر آخر. كذا ذكره الفارسي ويرد عليه لو قال لها اختاري مرتين فقط فإنه يقع بلا نية ولا
His saying: (If he said to her 'Ikhari, Ikhari' and she said 'I chose the first or the middle or the last,' triple divorce occurs without intention because his wording indicates intending divorce, which is multiplicity, and it pertains to divorce not to choosing the husband. The scholars differed regarding its occurrence in qada without intention with agreement that in reality it does not occur with intention. The author followed the master of al-Hidayah, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and al-Atabi in not requiring it for the reason we mentioned. Qadi Khan and Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi went to requiring it. It was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because repeating his command with choice does not make it apparent in divorce, since it is possible that he intended 'choose in property' and 'choose in dwelling' and the like. It is like 'I'tadi' (observe waiting period) if repeated. It may be answered that what is limited to three is divorce, not another matter. Thus al-Farisi mentioned it, and it is refuted that if he said 'Ikhari' only twice, it occurs without intention and...
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal issue of the husband repeating the word 'Ikhari' (choose) two or three times. The question is: if he says 'Ikhari, Ikhari' or 'Ikhari, Ikhari, Ikhari' and the wife chooses one of the instances (e.g., 'I chose the first'), does triple divorce occur? There is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Some scholars (like the author, following al-Hidayah, al-Sadr al-Shahid, and al-Atabi) hold that triple divorce occurs without the need for intention, because the repetition itself indicates that the husband intends divorce, and multiplicity pertains to divorce (which can be up to three) rather than to choosing the husband. Others (Qadi Khan and Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi) require intention for triple divorce, arguing that repetition does not make the intent of divorce apparent since the husband could have been referring to different things (e.g., choose in property, choose in dwelling). They analogize to saying 'I'tadi' (observe waiting period) repeatedly, which does not necessarily mean divorce. The preferred view in Fath al-Qadir is that intention is required. The passage also mentions a counter-argument: if the husband says 'Ikhari' only twice, even without intention, divorce occurs, which strengthens the view of those who do not require intention. The text is cut off, but the discussion continues regarding the case of two repetitions.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): The legal (court) ruling as distinguished from inner reality; in this context, the dispute is about occurrence in qada (legal ruling) without intention, while all agree it does not occur in reality (fī nafs al-amr) with intention.
اختياري (ikhtari): The imperative form of 'choose' used as a formula for delegation of divorce (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of the passage (following al-Hidayah), does the repetition of 'Ikhari' require the husband's intention for triple divorce to occur?
A) Yes, intention is required.
B) No, intention is not required.
C) It depends on the number of repetitions.
D) The author does not express a view.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a valid internal dispute on whether the repetition of 'Ikhari' automatically causes triple divorce; the mufta bihi view requires the husband's intention.

Linguistic Basis for Wife's Present Tense Response in Delegated Divorce
Analyzing the legal effect of the wife's present tense response as reporting an existing state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts the wife's present tense statement 'أنا أختار نفسي' as a valid divorce and distinguish it from a mere promise.

Core Idea
The present tense can report an existing state; the wife's 'I choose myself' effects divorce because it is treated as a report of a decision already made in the heart.

In delegated divorce (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq), the husband gives the wife the authority to divorce herself. A key question is what form her response must take. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the linguistic validity of the wife's present tense reply 'أنا أختار نفسي' and concludes that it effectively ends the marriage, based on the precedent of Aisha and the Arabic language's capacity for present tense to indicate current reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the husband's action and what response from the wife leads to divorce? The husband says 'اختياري' (Choose). The wife responds with 'أنا أختار نفسي' (I choose myself) or 'اخترت نفسي' (I chose myself). The ruling: she is divorced.
The response must be restricted to 'self' (نفس) – this is a condition.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof supports accepting the present tense response? The primary proof is the story of Aisha (رضي الله عنها), who responded with 'اخترت الله ورسوله' (I chose Allah and His Messenger) in the past tense, and the Prophet (ﷺ) accepted it as a valid choice.
This establishes that a response using choice (ikhtiyār) is effective.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the present tense 'أنا أختار' work here? In Hanafi linguistics, the present tense (muḍāri‘) is common between present and future. However, a contextual indicator (qarīna) – the fact that the choice resides in the heart (maḥallu'l-qalb) – allows it to be interpreted as a report of an existing state, not a future promise.
This is analogous to the testimony of faith (shahāda) where present tense affirms a current reality.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any dissenting view exist? The text notes that some schools might require explicit intention or past tense. The Hanafi school relies on the precedent of Aisha and the linguistic principle that present tense can function as a report of an existing state.
This is a legitimate area of ikhtilāf (scholarly difference).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is this the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position? The ruling is supported by clear precedent (Aisha), accepted by major Hanafi authorities like Al-Marghinani, and the linguistic argument (present tense as report) is considered sound. The position is consistent with the principle that a valid divorce occurs upon a clear choice.
The text also distinguishes from cases where the word 'أطلق' (I divorce) is used, which is not effective without custom (ta‘āruf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب تفويض الطلاق
٥٤٥
أحد كلاميهما شرط ولو قال لها اختاري فقالت أنا أختار نفسي أو اخترت نفسي تطلق
قد أفادها بقوله في أحد كلاميهما ليفيد أنه لا فرق بين الفعل الماضي والمضارع في جوابها المقيد بالنفس ليشير إلى أن لفظ «أنا مع المضارع ليس بشرط وإنما وقع بالمضارع وإن كان للوعد لقصة عائشة رضي الله عنها حيث أجابت بقولها اختار الله ورسوله واكتفى النبي به ، ولكون المضارع عندنا موضوعاً للحال والاستقبال فيه احتمال كما في كلمة الشهادة وأداء الشهادة فكان للتحقيق دون الوعد. وعلى اعتبار كونه مشتركاً بينهما فقد وجد هنا قرينة ترجح أحد مفهوميه وهو إمكان كونه إخباراً عن أمر قائم. في الحال لكون محله القلب فيصح الإخبار باللسان عما هو قائم بمحل آخر حال الإخبار. قيد بالإختيار لأنه لو قال طلقي نفسك فقالت أنا أطلق لا يقع، وكذا لو قال لعبده أعتق رقبتك فقال أنا أعتق لا يعتق لأنه لا يمكن جعله إخباراً عن طلاق قائم أو عتق قائم لأنه إنما يقوم باللسان، فلو حاز قام به الأمران في زمن واحد وهو محال. وفي فتح القدير : وهذا بناء على أن الإيقاع لا يكون بنفس «أطلق» لأنه لا تعارف فيه، وقدمنا أنه لو تعورف جاز ومقتضاه أنه يقع به هنا لو تعورف لأنه إنشاء لا إخبار ا هـ . وقد أخذه من الكافي والظهيرية حيث قالا : ولأن العادة لم تجر في «أنا طالق بإرادة الحال ا هـ . وفي المعراج : إلا إذا نوى إنشاء الطلاق فحينئذ يقع. فأنا وفي البزازية : لو قال أنا أحج لا يلزمه شيء بخلاف ما إذا قال إن شفى الله مريضي
قال
أحج كان نذراً لأن المواعيد باكتساب التعاليق تصير لازمة. وذكر في كتاب الكفالة : لو الذهب الذي لك على فلان أنا أدفعه أو أسلمه أو أقبضه مني لا يكون كفالة ما لم يقل لفظاً يدل على الوجوب كضمنت أو كفلت أو علي أو إلي. وهذا إذا ذكره منجزاً، أما إذا ذكره معلقاً بأن قال إن لم يؤده فلان فأنا أدفعه إليك أو نحوه يكون كفالة لما علم أن المواعيد باكتساب صور التعاليق تكون ،لازمة فإن قوله أنا أحج» لا يلزمه شيء، ولو علق وقال إن دخلت الدار فأنا أحج يلزمه الحج ا هـ . وفي البزازية : لو قالت له أنا أطلق نفسي لا يكون جواباً، ولو قالت اخترت أن أطلق نفسي كان جائزاً ا.هـ.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Delegation of Divorce. One of the two statements is a condition. If he said to her 'Choose', and she said 'I choose myself' or 'I chose myself', she is divorced. He benefited by saying 'in one of the two statements' to indicate that there is no difference between the past and present tense in her response restricted to 'self', to point out that the word 'I' with the present tense is not a condition, and that it occurred in the present tense even though it is for a promise, because of the story of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, where she responded with 'I choose Allah and His Messenger', and the Prophet accepted it. And because the present tense according to us is used for present and future, there is a possibility in it, as in the word of testimony and performance of testimony, so it is for certainty not promise. Considering it is common between them, here a contextual indicator has been found that weights one of its meanings: that it is possible that it is an report about an existent matter in the present moment because its place is the heart, so it is valid to report with the tongue about what exists in another place at the time of reporting. He restricted it to 'choice' because if he said 'Divorce yourself' and she said 'I divorce', it does not occur. Similarly, if he said to his slave 'Free your neck' and he said 'I free', he is not freed, because it cannot be made an report about an existent divorce or emancipation because it only occurs by the tongue. If it were possible, then two matters would be simultaneous in one moment, which is impossible. In Fath al-Qadir: This is based on the fact that initiation does not occur by the word 'I divorce' because there is no custom in it. And we have mentioned that if it were customary, it would be permissible. Its implication is that it would occur here if customary, because it is initiation not reporting. End. He took it from al-Kafi and al-Zahiriyya where they said: Because custom does not occur in 'I am divorced' intending the present state. End. In al-Mi'raj: Except if he intended to initiate divorce, then it occurs. So I say. In al-Bazzaziyya: If he said 'I perform Hajj', nothing becomes obligatory upon him, unlike if he said 'If Allah cures my sick', then said 'I perform Hajj', it becomes a vow because promises, by adopting suspended forms, become binding. And it is mentioned in Kitab al-Kafala: 'The gold which you have upon so-and-so, I will pay it' or 'hand it over' or 'receive it from me' is not a guarantee unless he says a word indicating obligation like 'I guarantee' or 'I stand surety' or 'upon me' or 'to me'. This is if he mentions it unconditionally. But if he mentions it as a condition by saying 'If so-and-so does not pay, then I will pay it to you' or similar, it becomes a guarantee, because it is known that promises, by adopting the forms of conditions, become binding. Then his saying 'I perform Hajj' does not obligate anything, but if he suspended and said 'If I enter the house, then I will perform Hajj' Hajj becomes obligatory. End. In al-Bazzaziyya: If she said to him 'I divorce myself', it is not a valid response. And if she said 'I choose to divorce myself', it is permissible. End.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling when a husband says 'اختياري' (choose) to his wife. The author explains that if the wife responds with 'أنا أختار نفسي' (I choose myself) in the present tense, or 'اخترت نفسي' (I chose myself) in the past tense, the divorce takes effect. The key proof is the story of Aisha, who, when given the choice, responded with 'اخترت الله ورسوله' (I choose Allah and His Messenger) in the past tense, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted that as a valid choice. The author then provides a linguistic analysis: the present tense in Arabic can indicate both present and future, but it is used here to report an existing state (that she has chosen divorce), not to promise a future act. This is analogous to the testimony of faith (shahada) where the present tense is used to affirm a current reality. The commentary also distinguishes between 'divorce yourself' and 'choose': if the husband says 'طلقي نفسك' (divorce yourself) and she says 'أنا أطلق' (I divorce), it does not work because the word 'أطلق' is not customary for initiating divorce; it is understood as a report of a future action. However, if there is a customary usage, it could be effective. The author also brings in examples from other areas of fiqh, such as vows and guarantees, to illustrate that promises become binding when tied to conditions. This reinforces the idea that the wife's response is not a mere promise but an actual report of a decision that effects divorce.

Key Terms
تفويض الطلاق (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq): Delegation of divorce where the husband gives the wife the authority to divorce herself.
اختيار (ikhtiyār): In this context, the choice given to the wife to either remain married or divorce herself.
مضارع (muḍāri‘): Present tense verb in Arabic, which can indicate present or future depending on context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'اختياري' and his wife responds 'أنا أختار نفسي', what is the ruling?
A) No divorce occurs because it is a future promise.
B) One divorce occurs because the present tense can report an existing state.
C) Three divorces occur because she expressed her choice.
D) It depends on her intention at the time.

Key Takeaway
The wife's present tense 'أنا أختار نفسي' effects a valid divorce in the Hanafi school because it is treated as a report of an existing decision, not a future promise.

Repetition of 'اختياري' and Dispute on Number of Divorces
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention and number of divorces in tafwid al-talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on both the requirement of intention and the number of divorces when 'اختياري' is repeated, and evaluate the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: three divorces; Sahibayn: one. Intention required in diyana, not in qada.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author examines a nuanced case of divorce by delegation where the husband repeats the word 'اختياري'. The discussion revolves around two intertwined issues: first, whether the husband's intention is necessary for the divorce to take effect in court; second, how many divorces occur when the wife responds with 'الأولى'. This intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples reveals the interplay between textual indications and necessary implications in deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key factual scenario
What does the husband say and what does the wife respond? Note the repetition of 'اختياري' and the wife's answer 'اخترت الأولى'.
2
Separate the two disputes
Distinguish between (1) whether the husband's intention (niyya) is required for the divorce to occur qada'an, and (2) how many divorces fall – three (Abu Hanifa) or one (Sahibayn).
The passage intertwines both; keep them analytically distinct.
3
Analyze the intention dispute
List the scholars who require intention (Qadikhan, al-Nasafi, preferred in Fath al-Qadir) and those who do not (author of al-Hidayah, al-Sadr al-Shahid). Understand the arguments: repetition may indicate divorce or something else. Also note the distinction between qada and diyana.
4
Analyze the number dispute
State the positions: Abu Hanifa says three divorces because the wife's response corresponds to each repetition; Sahibayn say one because 'الأولى' implies singularity and order. Examine the talil (reasoning) about necessary implications.
The key is whether singularity is a necessary implication or an independent meaning.
5
Connect to practical ruling
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, bain divorce; under Sahibayn, raj'i divorce. Also note the mu'tamad on intention: required in diyana but not in qada according to the author's preference.

لمفرد مرتب .
His saying: (And if he said to her 'Choose, choose' and she said 'I chose the first' or 'the middle' or 'the last', then three divorces occur without intention, because in his wording there is an indication of the desire for divorce, and that is multiplicity, and that only relates to divorce not to choosing the husband. The scholars differed regarding its occurrence judicially (qada'an) without intention, while agreeing that in reality it does not occur without intention. The author, following the author of Al-Hidayah, Al-Sadr al-Shahid, and al-‘Attabi, holds that intention is not required for the reasons mentioned. Qadikhan and Abu al-Ma'in al-Nasafi held that it is required. Fath al-Qadir preferred the latter because repeating the command to choose does not become apparent in divorce, since he might intend 'choose in wealth' or 'choose in residence' and the like. It is like saying 'Count your idda' if he repeats it. It may be answered that what is limited to three is divorce, not another matter. This is mentioned by al-Farisi. It is countered that if he said to her 'choose' twice only, it occurs without intention and without [mention of self]. End. It contradicts what is limited. In Talkhis al-Jami‘ al-Kabir: The number is specific to divorce, so it suffices from mentioning self and intention in its origin. It has been transmitted from Ghayat al-Bayan that what is explicitly stated in al-Jami‘ al-Kabir is the requirement of intention. He said: It is apparent. End. The upshot is that the relied-upon, both in transmission and understanding, is the requirement of intention (niyya) without requiring the mention of self (nafs). His absolute statement indicates that mention of self is not required in either of the two statements, like intention, because repetition stands in its place as we have mentioned. It is said that mention of self is necessary, but it was omitted due to its fame, because Muhammad's purpose was merely to derive subsidiary rulings without explaining the validity of the response. Thus in al-Kafi. Then, the occurrence of three here is the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: One divorce occurs, considering that this word indicates order and singularity. When the first fails due to the impossibility of order in what is gathered in one's ownership, it is not permissible to nullify the other, so it must be considered. His (the Imam's) argument is that it indicates order and singularity as a necessary implication. So when the primary fails, the subsidiary fails. It was objected that singularity is not a necessary implication; rather, each is its meaning, and one is not subsidiary to the other. Therefore al-Tahawi chose the view of the two. It was answered: Granted that singularity is a meaning, but it is not necessary that it is intended. Because one part of the associated meaning may be intended and the other subsidiary, as is intended here. Because the description is placed for the essence by virtue of a meaning that is intended; thus singularity is not considered in it, whether real or figurative, like the first group and the first congregation, except for the one described by that relation. So if the primary is nullified, the speech is nullified. He restricted it by his saying 'I chose the first' and what is conjoined with it, because if she said 'I chose one divorce, the first', one divorce occurs by agreement. Thus in al-Mi‘raj. And if she said 'I chose' or 'I chose his choice' or 'the choice' or 'once by once' or 'once' or 'single' or 'one choice', then three divorces occur according to their view. And if the husband said 'I intended by the first divorce and by the others confirmation'. His saying: (And no limitation) meaning that there is no limitation of divorce to two. His saying: (And the upshot that the relied-upon etc.) The commentator Miskeen said: Sheikh Qasim inclined to not needing intention in qada, but regarding occurrence between him and Allah, intention is required. End. I say: Al-Maqdisi elaborated in his commentary on this point then said: Reliance is on what the author mentioned: no requirement of intention and mention of self in qada, but in diyana intention is necessary. End. I say: This creates a problem on what the author mentioned regarding preferring requirement of intention without self: if repetition does not indicate desire for divorce such that intention is required, then mention of self should be required because... [text unclear]. The one who holds that repetition does not stand in place of self says that mention of self or what stands in its place is necessary to specify desire for divorce, like 'al-ikhtiyara' and the like, and he requires intention. His saying: (Considering that this word) i.e. her saying 'I chose the first' etc. For 'first', 'middle', and 'last' each is a name for a singular ordered entity.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage deals with a more complex scenario: the husband repeats the word 'اختياري' (choose) two or three times, and the wife responds with 'اخترت الأولى' (I chose the first) etc. The author discusses two key issues. First, whether the husband's intention (niyya) is required for the divorce to be effective in court (qada'an). Some scholars, like the author of Al-Hidayah, hold that no intention is needed because the repetition itself indicates the husband's desire for divorce. Others, like Qadikhan, require intention. The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) according to the later scholars is that intention is required, but the mention of 'self' (nafs) is not necessary because repetition serves that purpose. There is also a discussion about the number of divorces: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that three divorces occur because the wife's response 'اخترت الأولى' corresponds to the three commands. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), hold that only one divorce occurs because the word 'الأولى' (the first) implies singularity, and when the first fails due to the impossibility of sequential divorces in a single moment, only one remains. The Hanafi position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, but the commentary notes a difference between qada (court) and diyana (conscience) regarding intention. In court, the divorce is enforced without requiring the husband to prove intention, but between him and Allah, he must have intended divorce.

Key Terms
تكرار (takrār): Repetition of the word 'اختياري' by the husband.
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart; required for certain acts of divorce according to some Hanafi scholars.
قضاء (qaḍā’): Judicial ruling; what is enforced by the court based on apparent evidence.
ديانة (diyānatan): Between the individual and Allah; based on inner reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a husband repeatedly says 'اختياري' and the wife responds 'اخترت الأولى', what is the ruling on the number of divorces according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa: three divorces; Sahibayn: one divorce.
B) Imam Abu Hanifa: one divorce; Sahibayn: three divorces.
C) Both agree it is one divorce.
D) Both agree it is three divorces.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tafwid al-talaq, repeated 'اختياري' leads to one or three divorces depending on whether singularity is seen as necessary implication; intention is required in diyana but not in qada, and mention of self is not necessary due to repetition.

Talaq — Divorce

The Sahibayn vs. Imam: One Divorce or Three from 'I Choose the First'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on linguistic interpretation of 'الأولى'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the phrase 'اخترت الأولى' in delegated divorce, explain the linguistic reasoning (order vs. individuality) behind each view, and identify the agreed exception when 'تطليقة' is specified.

Core Idea
The word 'الأولى' splits the Sahibayn from Imam: one divorce or three hinges on whether 'individuality' stands alone or falls with 'order'.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on delegated divorce (تفويض الطلاق). When a husband gives his wife the power to divorce herself and she says 'اخترت الأولى' (I choose the first), does she get one divorce or three? The answer depends on a subtle linguistic analysis of the word 'الأولى'. We will trace how Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) derive opposite rulings from the same word, and what practical difference this makes for the couple's marital status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Phrase and Context
The wife says 'اخترت الأولى' after the husband has delegated the divorce option (e.g., by saying 'اختاري'). Recognize that this is a delegation of divorce, not a general choice of marriage.
2
Unpack the Dual Meanings of 'الأولى'
The word 'الأولى' can indicate both order (ترتيب) – being first in a series – and individuality (إفراد) – being a single unit. The dispute centers on whether these meanings are independent or one is subsidiary to the other.
Also note the word 'أولى' is feminine singular; it refers to a divorce not mentioned explicitly.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's Reasoning
The Sahibayn argue that both meanings are inherent in the word. Since order is impossible here (you cannot have a 'first' divorce when the series is not yet formed), the order aspect becomes invalid, but the individuality meaning remains valid, resulting in one divorce.
They see الإفراد as an independent meaning, not dependent on الترتيب.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's Reasoning
Imam argues that individuality is a necessary consequence (ضرورة) of order. When the primary meaning (order) fails, the subsidiary meaning (individuality) also fails. Both are invalid, so the default applies – three divorces (since the delegation allowed up to three).
Imam's view is that both meanings are interdependent; if order fails, the word becomes meaningless, so the full number of possible divorces (three) is presumed.
5
Apply the Agreed Exception
If the wife explicitly says 'اخترت تطليقة الأولى' (I choose the first divorce), all scholars agree it is one divorce. This exception confirms that the dispute is purely about the semantic interpretation of 'الأولى' alone.
This also highlights that specifying 'تطليقة' removes the ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب تفويض الطلاق
اهـ. وهو مخالف لما حصر. وفي تلخيص الجامع الكبير والعدد خاص بالطلاق فأغنى عن ذكر النفس والنية في أصله فقد نقل في غاية البيان أن المصرح به في الجامع الكبير اشتراط النية قال : وهو الظاهر ا.هـ. والحاصل أن المعتمد رواية ودراية اشتراطها دون اشتراط ذکر النفس. وأفاد بإطلاقه عدم اشتراط ذكر النفس في أحد كلاميهما كالنية لأن التكرار قام مقامه لما قدمناه . وقيل : لا بد من ذكر النفس وإنما حذف لشهرته لأن غرض محمد مجرد التفريع دون بيان صحة الجواب. كذا في الكافي. ثم وقوع الثلاث هنا قول الإمام. وقالا : يقع واحدة نظراً إلى أن هذه الكلمة تفيد الترتيب والإفراد فإذا بطل الأول لاستحالة الترتيب في المجتمع في الملك لم يجز إبطال الآخر فوجب اعتباره وله أنها تفيد الترتيب والإفراد من ضرورته، فإذا بطل في حق الأصل بطل في حق التبع، وقد منع أن الإفراد من ضرورته بل كل منهما مدلوله وليس أحدهما تبعاً للآخر ولذا اختار الطحاوي قولهما. وأجيب عنه سلمنا أن الفردية مدلولة لكن لا يلزم أن تكون مقصودة لأنه قد يكون أحد جزئي المدلول المطابق هو المقصود والآخر تبعاً كما هو المراد هنا لأن الوصف وضع للذات باعتبار معنى هو المقصود فلم تلاحظ الفردية فيه حقيقياً أو اعتبارياً كالطائفة الأولى والجماعة الأولى إلا من هو متصف بتلك النسبة، فإذا بطلت بطل الكلام قيد بقوله «اخترت الأولى» وما عطف عليه لأنها لو قالت اخترت لتطليقة الأولى وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً. كذا في المعراج. ولو قالت اخترت أو اخترت اختياره أو الاختيارة أو مرة بمرة أو دفعة أو بدفعة أو بواحدة أو اختيارة واحدة يقع الثلاث في قولهم، ولو قال الزوج نويت بالأولى طلاقاً وبالأخريين التأكيد.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Delegation of Divorce. End. And it contradicts what was restricted. And in Talkhis al-Jami' al-Kabir: 'And the number is specific to divorce, so it suffices from mentioning the self and intention in its origin.' It was narrated in Ghayat al-Bayan that what is explicitly stated in al-Jami' al-Kabir is the condition of intention. He said: and that is apparent. The conclusion is that the relied-upon, in both transmission and knowledge, is its condition without the condition of mentioning the self. And his absolute statement indicates the lack of condition of mentioning the self in one of his two statements like intention because repetition takes its place as we have previously stated. And it is said: mentioning the self is necessary, but it was omitted due to its fame because Muhammad's purpose is merely subdivision without explaining the correctness of the answer. Thus in al-Kafi. Then the occurrence of three here is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: one occurs, considering that this word indicates order and individuality. So when the first is invalid due to the impossibility of order in what is combined in possession, it is not permissible to invalidate the other, so it must be considered. And for him (Imam), it indicates order and individuality as a necessary consequence, so when it is invalid with respect to the original, it is invalid with respect to the subsidiary. And it is denied that individuality is a necessary consequence; rather, each is its meaning, and neither is subsidiary to the other. Therefore al-Tahawi chose their view. And it is answered: we concede that individuality is its meaning, but it does not necessarily follow that it is intended, because one of the two parts of the denotation may be intended and the other subsidiary, as is intended here, because the description is placed for the entity by virtue of a meaning that is intended, so individuality is not considered in it either realistically or by consideration, like the first group and the first congregation, except for the one who is described by that relation. So when it becomes invalid, the speech becomes invalid, restricted by his saying 'I chose the first' and what is conjoined to it, because if she said 'I chose the first divorce,' one divorce occurs by agreement. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And if she said 'I chose' or 'I chose his choice' or 'the choice' or 'once by once' or 'at once' or 'by one' or 'one choice,' three occur in their statement. And if the husband said 'I intended by the first a divorce and by the last two emphasis'.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal effect of a wife's statement 'اخترت الأولى' (I choose the first) when the husband has delegated the power of divorce to her. The central issue is whether this statement results in three divorces (Imam Abu Hanifa's view) or one divorce (the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, known as the Sahibayn). The passage begins by discussing the requirement of intention (نية) and whether mentioning the self (النفس) is needed. It concludes that the relied-upon position is that intention is required but not mentioning the self, as repetition of the word 'اخترت' serves the same purpose. Then the dispute is presented: The Sahibayn argue that the word 'الأولى' implies both order (ترتيب) and individuality (إفراد). Since order is impossible in the context of multiple divorces (because a single divorce cannot be 'first' in a series), the order aspect becomes invalid, but the individuality remains, so only one divorce occurs. Imam Abu Hanifa responds that individuality is a necessary consequence of order, so when order fails, individuality also fails, resulting in three divorces. The passage further notes that if the wife explicitly says 'اخترت تطليقة الأولى' (I choose the first divorce), all agree it is one divorce. The dispute is restricted to when she says 'اخترت الأولى' without specifying 'تطليقة'. The discussion also touches on various other phrasings like 'اخترت اختياره' etc., where the ruling is three divorces by agreement. The passage ends with a note about the husband's intention if he says he meant emphasis.

Key Terms
تفويض الطلاق (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq): Delegation of the power to divorce to the wife by the husband's statement such as 'اختاري' or 'أمرك بيدك'.
اخترت الأولى (akhtartu al-ūlā): The wife's statement meaning 'I choose the first' when given the option to divorce herself.
الإفراد (al-ifrād): Individuality; the quality of being a single unit or individual.
الترتيب (al-tartīb): Order; being sequentially arranged (e.g., first, second, third).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does the wife's statement 'اخترت الأولى' result in one divorce instead of three?
A) Because the word 'الأولى' only means 'the first' and thus refers to one divorce.
B) Because the word indicates both order and individuality; order is impossible, but individuality remains.
C) Because the husband's delegation was limited to one divorce.
D) Because the wife's intention was only one divorce.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'اخترت الأولى' yields one divorce per the Sahibayn and three per Imam Abu Hanifa, because of differing analyses of whether 'individuality' is an independent meaning or a necessary consequence of 'order'.

Repeated Delegation of Divorce with a Money Condition
Rulings on repeating 'اخترتي' three times with money.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on repeated delegation of divorce with a money condition and determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for each scenario.

Core Idea
When a husband repeats 'اخترتي' three times with a money condition, the money is due fully only if the repetitions are a single offer (Imam) or only on the last choice (Sahibayn).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a common scenario in Hanafi divorce law: a husband says 'اخترتي' three times to his wife, and stipulates a sum of money (e.g., a thousand dirhams) for the delegation. The wife then chooses herself. How many divorces occur, and is she obliged to pay the full amount? Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ on whether the money is due when she chooses the first or second option. This lesson will walk you through their reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The husband repeats 'اخترتي' three times, with a money condition (e.g., 'بألف'). The wife accepts and then chooses herself (e.g., by saying 'اخترت نفسي'). Determine the number of divorces and whether the money is binding.
The phrase 'اخترتي' is a delegation (tafwid) allowing her to divorce herself.
2
State the two positions
According to Abu Hanifa, three divorces occur and the full money is due regardless of which option she chose. According to the Sahibayn, three divorces occur but the money is due only if she chose the last option.
If she chose the first or middle, the money is not due according to Sahibayn.
3
Trace the reasoning
Abu Hanifa views the three repetitions as a single offer; the money condition attaches to the entire delegation. The Sahibayn view each repetition as an independent offer; the money is mentioned only with the last, so it is tied only to that choice.
This is a linguistic/structural difference in how the speech is interpreted.
4
Apply to variations with conjunctions
If the repetitions are linked by 'و' or 'ف', Abu Hanifa still rules three divorces with full money. The Sahibayn rule that the entire speech becomes one offer; if she divorces only once, only one divorce occurs and no money is due.
Conjunctions unify the statement, changing the ruling for Sahibayn.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if she chooses the first option, Abu Hanifa would require full payment; the Sahibayn would require nothing. This affects whether the wife incurs financial liability.
Later Hanafi works may prefer one view; both are valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قالت اخترت أو اخترت اختياره أو الاختيارة أو مرة بمرة أو دفعة أو بدفعة أو بواحدة أو اختيارة واحدة يقع الثلاث في قولهم، ولو قال الزوج نويت بالأولى طلاقاً وبالأخريين التأكيد لا يصدق قضاء. كذا في المحيط والأصل أنها إذا ذكرت الأولى أو ما يجري مجراها فهو على ثلاثة أوجه : فإن قالت اخترت التطليقة الأولى وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً، وإن قالت اخترت الاختيارة الأولى فثلاث اتفاقاً والخلاف فيما إذا لم تذكر المنعوت. وأورد المصنف تكرار التخيير ثلاثاً، سواء كان بلا عطف كما ذكره أو به من واو أو فاء أو «ثم» لأنه جواب الكل حتى لو كان بمال لزم كله. وفي شرح تلخيص الجامع للفارسي : إلا أن في العطف بـ«ثم» لو الجامع : لو قال لها اختاري اختاري اختاري بألف أو عطف فقالت اخترت طلقت ثلاثاً بألف وفاء بإطلاق الجواب فقبلت فور أنواع تمليك والعدد خاص بالطلاق فأغنى عن ذكر النفس والنية، كذا اخترت لواحدة أو واحدة حذار التخيير بالشك إذ ينعت بها الدفعة والاختيارة، وفي اخترت تطليقة لا يقع للعطف لأنها للفرد وهو ببعض الألف ضرر بخلاف جانبها وبالكلمة إيجاب لا جواب بخلاف الوكيل إذ عليه الوفاق لا الجواب وفي غيره يقع فرد ولا مال ما لم تعن الثالثة لخصوصه بها، كذا اخترت الأول عندهما إذا أضمر الطلقة حفظاً للنعت، وعنده يقع الثلاث إذا أضمر الاختيارة حفظاً للأصل بتطليق الجواب والصدر ا.هـ. وأفاد المصنف بوقوع الثلاث أنه لو كان بنفسه ولم يذكر معه حرف الجمع والبدل لم يذكر إلا في الأخيرة فلا يجب إلا باختيار الأخيرة، ولو ذكر بالواو أو الفاء فعند أبي حنيفة لا يختلف الجواب فيقع الثلاث ويلزمها الألف، وعندهما لا يقع الطلاق في هذه الثالثة بالألف لأنه قرن المال بالأخيرة ولم يذكر حرف العطف بينهما ليصير المقرون بالأخيرة مقروناً بالأولى والثانية وهذا كالاستثناء والشرط فإنه ينصرف إلى الأخيرة ا هـ قوله : (ولو قالت طلقت نفسي أو اخترت And if she said 'I chose' or 'I chose his choice' or 'the choice' or 'once by once' or 'at once' or 'by one' or 'one choice,' three occur in their statement. And if the husband said 'I intended by the first a divorce and by the last two emphasis,' he is not believed judicially. Thus in al-Muhit. And the principle is that if she mentions 'the first' or what runs in its course, it is on three aspects: if she said 'I chose the first divorce,' one divorce occurs by agreement. If she said 'I chose the first choice,' then three by agreement. And the dispute is when she does not mention the described. And the author mentioned repetition of choice three times, whether without conjunction as he mentioned or with it by waw, fa, or thumma, because it is the answer of all, even if it were with money, it all becomes binding. And in Sharh Talkhis al-Jami' for al-Farisi: except that with conjunction by thumma if she chooses herself by the first before the husband speaks the second and third and she is not consummated, she becomes irrevocably divorced by the first and nothing else occurs. And in al-Walwaljiyyah: if he said to her 'your affair is in your hand' intending three: 'your affair is in your hand for a thousand dirhams' intending three, and she accepted that, then said 'I have chosen myself by the first option.' Abu Hanifa said: she is divorced three times and the money is binding on her, and her mention of the first is irrelevant. And the two (Sahibayn) said: she is divorced three times and the money is not binding on her, and her mention of the first is not irrelevant. And in Talkhis al-Jami': if he said 'choose, choose, choose' with a thousand or conjunction, and she said 'I chose,' she is divorced three times with a thousand, fulfilling the absolute answer, so she accepted immediately as types of ownership, and the number is specific to divorce, so it suffices from mentioning the self and intention. Similarly, 'I chose' for one or one, caution of choice by doubt, because it is described by the instant and the choice. And in 'I chose a divorce' it does not occur due to conjunction, because it is for the individual, and it is harmful with part of a thousand, unlike her side, and with the word it is a positive affirmation, not an answer, unlike the agent, because upon him is agreement, not answer. And in other than that, one occurs and no money unless she intends the third due to its specificity. Similarly, 'I chose the first' according to the two (Sahibayn) if she implies the divorce to preserve the description, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) three occur if she implies the choice to preserve the origin by divorcing the answer and the beginning. The author indicated by the occurrence of three that if it were with money, all the money is binding on her as we have previously stated, and it is the statement of Imam. And according to the two, if she chooses herself by the last, all the money is binding on her, and if she chooses herself by the first or middle, nothing is binding because each of the choices is a separate choice, for it is complete speech by itself, and the collective conjunction and substitution were not mentioned except in the last, so it is only obligatory by choosing the last. And if he mentioned by waw or fa, then according to Abu Hanifa the answer does not differ: three occur and the thousand is binding. According to the two, divorce does not occur in this form because all becomes one speech by the collective conjunction, so it becomes as if he said to her 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand' and she divorced one. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Kafi: if he repeated without conjunction and she said 'I choose myself by all,' the first two occur without anything, and in the third with the thousand because he coupled the money with the last and did not mention the conjunction between them so that what is coupled with the last is coupled with the first and second, and this is like exception and condition, for it applies to the last. His statement: (And if she said 'I divorced myself' or 'I chose myself' with one divorce, she becomes irrevocably divorced by one) meaning in answer to his saying 'choose.' And it is valid as an answer because divorce is included within the choice, so she has brought some of what was delegated to her, as if he said 'Divorce yourself three times' and she divorced one, unlike...
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on delegated divorce, focusing on cases where the phrase 'اخترتي' is repeated three times, with or without conjunctions, and where a monetary sum is stipulated (e.g., a thousand dirhams). The author presents multiple scenarios and the differing opinions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Key points: (1) If the husband repeats 'اخترتي' three times without conjunction, and the wife responds by choosing a specific one (e.g., 'I choose the first'), the ruling differs based on intent and wording. (2) If the husband says 'اخترتي' three times with a money stipulation (e.g., 'for a thousand dirhams'), and the wife accepts and then chooses herself, the money becomes due according to Imam Abu Hanifa regardless of which option she chooses, while the Sahibayn hold that the money is only due if she chooses the last option because each repetition is a separate offer and the money is only attached to the last. (3) If the repetitions are linked with conjunctions like 'و' or 'ف', Imam Abu Hanifa still rules three divorces and the money due, while the Sahibayn rule that the entire speech becomes one offer, and if she only divorces once, only one divorce occurs and the money is not due. (4) Additional nuances: if the wife says 'اخترت تطليقة' (I choose a divorce), it counts as one; if she says 'اخترت الاختيارة الأولى' (I choose the first choice), it counts as three by agreement. The passage also cites al-Walwaljiyyah for a case where the husband says 'أمرك بيدك' with an intention of three and a money condition, and the wife's response. The passage ends with a note on the wife saying 'طلقت نفسي' (I divorced myself) in response to 'اخترتي', which is valid as it is a partial fulfillment of the delegation.

Key Terms
التخيير (al-takhyīr): Giving the wife the choice to divorce herself, often by saying 'اخترتي' or 'أمرك بيدك'.
البدل (al-badal): The monetary consideration (e.g., 1000 dirhams) stipulated in the delegation of divorce.
المنعوت (al-man‘ūt): The described term; in this context, the specific term like 'تطليقة' or 'اختيارة' that is explicitly mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'اختاري اختاري اختاري على ألف' without conjunctions, and the wife says 'اخترت نفسي بالثانية', what is the ruling per the view of the Sahibayn?
A) Three divorces, full money due.
B) Three divorces, no money due.
C) One divorce, full money due.
D) Two divorces, half money due.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's ruling on repeated delegation of divorce with a money condition depends on whether the repetition is seen as a single offer (Imam) or multiple offers (Sahibayn), affecting the wife's financial liability.

Specification and Conjunction in Repeated Tafwid
Explains rulings on repeated delegation of divorce with specification and conjunction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings when a wife specifies 'first divorce' vs 'first option' in repeated tafwid, and apply the Hanafi positions on the binding effect of wealth when the wife chooses early.

Core Idea
In repeated tafwid, specifying 'first option' yields three divorces by consensus; ambiguous mention of 'first' triggers dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a subtle point in the law of delegated divorce (tafwid). When a husband says 'choose' multiple times, and the wife responds by picking the 'first', the outcome hinges on whether she means the first divorce or the first option. Furthermore, if the delegation was tied to a payment of money, the timing of her choice and the conjunction used affect whether the wealth becomes binding. Let's work through the scenarios step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the repeated tafwid and the wife's response
Recognize that the husband said 'Ikhtari' three times and the wife replied by selecting the first, middle, or last. The divorce falls, and the husband's denial is not accepted.
This establishes the baseline: a valid occurrence of talaq.
2
Distinguish between specification types
If the wife says 'I chose the first divorce' (التطليقة الأولى), one divorce occurs by consensus. If she says 'I chose the first option' (الاختيارة الأولى), three divorces occur by consensus. The dispute arises when she says only 'the first' without qualification.
The key is the Arabic term used: 'tatliqa' vs 'ikhtiyara'.
3
Analyze the effect of conjunction on the delegation
Repeating 'choose' without conjunction or with waw, fa, or thumma makes the entire response binding, including any wealth promised. However, with 'thumma', if the wife chooses herself before the husband finishes speaking, only the first is effective (if she is non-consummated).
Conjunction type affects whether the delegations are integrated or separate.
4
Examine the Walwaljiya case with wealth condition
The husband says 'Your affair is in your hand for one thousand dirhams' intending three. The wife accepts and later says 'I have chosen myself with the first option.' Abu Hanifa says she is divorced three times and owes the full amount; the Sahibayn agree on three divorces but hold she owes nothing.
The dispute centers on whether her mention of 'first' is meaningful or null.
5
Compare Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn on the meaning of 'first'
Abu Hanifa views the three delegations as one integrated command, so choosing the 'first option' triggers all three. The Sahibayn view each repetition as a separate delegation, so 'first' refers only to the first delegation, which had no wealth condition.
The practical consequence is a difference of 1000 dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال لها اختاري اختاري اختاري فقالت اخترت الأولى أو الوسطى أو الأخيرة وقع ثم قال لا يصدق قضاء. كذا في المحيط والأصل أنها إذا ذكرت الأولى أو ما يجري مجراها فهو على ثلاثة أوجه : فإن قالت اخترت التطليقة الأولى وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً، وإن قالت اخترت الاختيارة الأولى فثلاث اتفاقاً والخلاف فيما إذا لم تذكر المنعوت. وأورد المصنف تكرار التخيير ثلاثاً، سواء كان بلا عطف كما ذكره أو به من واو أو فاء أو «ثم» لأنه جواب الكل حتى لو كان بمال لزم كله. وفي شرح تلخيص الجامع للفارسي : إلا أن في العطف بـ«ثم» لو اختارت نفسها بالأولى قبل أن يتكلم الزوج بالثانية والثالثة وهي غير مدخول بها بانت بالأولى ولم يقع بغيرها شيء ا هـ . وفي الولوالجية : لو قال لها أمرك بيدك ينوي ثلاثاً : لها أمرك بيدك على ألف درهم ينوي ثلاثاً فقبلت ذلك ثم قالت قد اخترت نفسي بالخيار الأول. قال أبو حنيفة: هي طالق ثلاثاً والمال لازم عليها وذكرها الأول لغو. وقالا : هي طالق ثلاثاً ولا يلزمها المال وذكرها الأول ليس بلغو ا هـ
And if he said to her: 'Choose, choose, choose,' and she said: 'I chose the first, or the middle, or the last,' then it falls. Then he said: He is not believed in court. So it is in al-Muhit. And the principle is that if she mentions 'the first' or its equivalent, then it is in three ways: If she says 'I chose the first divorce,' one divorce falls by agreement. And if she says 'I chose the first option,' three fall by agreement. And the dispute is when she does not mention the qualified. And the author mentioned the repetition of the option three times, whether it is without conjunction as he mentioned, or with waw, fa, or thumma, because it is a response to all, so even if it is with wealth, it all becomes binding. And in Sharh Talkhis al-Jami' by al-Farisi: Except that in conjunction with thumma, if she chose herself with the first before the husband spoke the second and third, and she is not consummated, she is irrevocably divorced by the first and nothing else falls. End quote. And in al-Walwaljiya: If he said to her: 'Your affair is in your hand' intending three, and he said: 'Your affair is in your hand for one thousand dirhams' intending three, and she accepted that, then she said: 'I have chosen myself with the first option.' Abu Hanifa said: She is divorced three times and the wealth is binding upon her, and her mention of 'first' is null. And the two said: She is divorced three times and the wealth is not binding upon her, and her mention of 'first' is not null. End quote.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute explaining rulings on repeated delegation of divorce (tafwid) with specification and conjunction. It opens by stating that if a husband says 'choose' three times and the wife responds by choosing the first, middle, or last, the divorce falls and the husband's denial is not accepted in court. The author then explains three scenarios when the wife specifies: if she says 'I chose the first divorce,' one divorce occurs by consensus; if she says 'I chose the first option,' three divorces occur by consensus. The dispute arises when she does not mention 'the qualified' (al-man'ut), i.e., she says only 'the first' without specifying whether she means the divorce or the option. Next, the author discusses the effect of conjunction: repeating 'choose' without a conjunction or with waw, fa, or thumma makes the entire response binding, including any wealth promised. However, there is an exception from al-Farisi: if the conjunction is thumma and the wife chooses herself with the first before the husband finishes speaking, and she is not yet consummated, only the first is effective. Finally, a case from al-Walwaljiya is cited: the husband says 'your affair is in your hand' intending three, adds a condition of one thousand dirhams, and the wife chooses herself with the first option. Abu Hanifa rules that she is divorced three times and must pay the full amount, as her mention of 'first' is meaningless; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on three divorces but hold that she owes nothing because 'first' is meaningful and refers to the first delegation only.

Key Terms
التطليقة (al-tatliqa): A single divorce; the individual act of divorce.
الاختيارة (al-ikhtiyara): The option or choice itself; when a wife says 'I chose the first option,' it implies she is choosing the entire delegated authority, resulting in three divorces.
المنعوت (al-man'ut): The qualified term; if the wife says 'the first' without specifying whether it is the divorce or the option, the ruling is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says 'choose' three times, and the wife says 'I chose the first option' (اخترت الاختيارة الأولى), how many divorces occur?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
In repeated tafwid, the wife's specification of 'first divorce' gives one, 'first option' gives three; ambiguous 'first' is disputed, and the Walwaljiya case shows the Sahibayn view that wealth is not binding on early choice.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Ba'in vs Raj'i in Tafwid Self-Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether tafwid self-divorce is ba'in or raj'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a wife's self-divorce in tafwid is ba'in or raj'i, and identify the mufta bihi position with its supporting evidence.

Core Idea
In tafwid, the husband's delegation controls; the stronger view holds the divorce is ba'in, not raj'i.

This passage delves into an important dispute within the Hanafi school on the nature of divorce when a wife exercises delegated authority (tafwid). While the husband grants her the option to divorce herself, the type of divorce that results—whether irrevocable (ba'in) or revocable (raj'i)—has been a point of contention between two narrations. The passage clarifies that the majority opinion, supported by many authoritative texts, rules that it is ba'in.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
State the disagreement about the type of divorce when wife says 'I divorced myself' in response to 'choose'.
2
Present the majority Hanafi position and its proof
The majority (zahir al-riwayah) holds it is ba'in. Proof: husband's delegation controls; comparison if he ordered a specific type and she did otherwise.
Key principle: لا عبرة لإيقاعها بل لتفويض الزوج
3
Present the opposing narration
Sadr al-Islam's Jami' considers it raj'i, looking at the wife's execution.
This narration is from certain copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir.
4
Trace the tarjih (preference)
Sharh al-Wiqaya and later texts (al-Nahr, al-Kafi) prefer ba'in as asahh, citing majority of sources like al-Jami' al-Kabir.
The passage resolves that what is in al-Hidaya is one of the two narrations, not a mistake.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If raj'i, husband can take her back during idda; if ba'in, he cannot and must remarry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قالت طلقت نفسي أو اخترت نفسي بتطليقة بانت بواحدة) يعني في جواب قوله اختاري وإنما صلح جواباً له لأن التطليق داخل في ضمن التخيير فقد أتت ببعض ما فوض إليها كما لو قال طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً فطلقت واحدة بخلاف الثلاث بلا نية ولو قالت طلقت نفسي أو اخترت نفسي بتطليقة بانت بواحدة أمرك وهو مخالف ما لو قالت اخترت نفسي في جواب طلقي نفسك لأن الاختيار لم يفوض إليها لا قصداً ولا ضمناً. وإنما وقع به البائن دون الرجعي وإن كان صريحاً لأنه لا عبرة. لإيقاعها بل لتفويض الزوج ، ألا ترى أنه لو أمرها بالبائن أو الرجعي فعكست وقع ما أمر به الزوج، وقد ذكر صدر الإسلام في جامعه أنه يقع به الرجعي نظراً لما أوقعته المرأة لعامة الكتب لكن في شرح الوقاية أن في المسألة روايتين : في رواية تقع رجعية وفي أخرى بائنة وهذا أصح ا هـ . وبهذا ظهر أن ما في الهداية إحدى الروايتين فقول الشارح إنه غلط وابن الهمام إنه سهو ومما لا ينبغي أن يقال في مثله ولذا قال في الكافي : إن ما في الهداية موجود في بعض نسخ الجامع الصغير والصواب أنه لا يملك الرجعة كما في الجامع الكبير ا هـ . قيدنا بكونه جواباً لقوله اختاري لأنه لو كرر اختاري ثلاثاً بألف فقالت اخترت نفسي بتطليقة أو اخترت تطليقة لم يقع شيء في صورة العطف لأن التطليقة تصلح للفرد دون الثلاث ووقوع الواحدة ممتنع دفعاً للضرر عنه ووقعت واحدة بائنة في غير صورة العطف اتفاقاً، ولا يجب عليها شيء من المال إن قالت عنيت التطليقة الأولى أو الثانية، وإن قالت عنيت الثالثة لزمها كل الألف بخصوص المال بالثالثة. كذا في شرح التلخيص وهو شرح لما قدمناه وعنه في المحيط : ولو قال اختاري فقالت فعلت لا يقع لأن هذا كناية عن قولها اخترت وبه لا يقع فكذا هذا ولو قال اختاري نفسك فقالت فعلت يقع لما بينا ا هـ . وفي جامع الفصولين لو قال بعت أمرك منك بألف فاختارت نفسها في المجلس بانت ولزمها المال ا هـ . قوله : (أمرك بيدك في تطليقة أو اختاري تطليقة فاختارت نفسها طلقت رجعية) لأنه جعل لها الاختيار بتطليقة وهي معقبة للرجعة والمقيد للبينونة إذا قرن بالصريح صار رجعياً. قوله: (وقد ذكر صدر الإسلام الخ) قال في النهر : وما وقع في الهداية من أنه يملك الرجعة قال الشارحون إنه غلط من الكتاب والأصح من الرواية فهي واحدة ولا يملك الرجعة لأن روايات المبسوط والجامع الكبير والزيادات وعامة نسخ الجامع الصغير هكذا سوى الجامع الصغير لصدر الإسلام فإنه ذكر فيه مثل ما ذكر في الكتاب كذا في العناية. وأقول: كيف يكون ما في الهداية غلطاً من الكتاب وقد علل المسألة بأن هذا اللفظ يوجب الانطلاق بعد انقضاء العدة فكأنها اختارت نفسها بعد العدة، فالصواب كما في الشرح اطلاق كونه غلطاً. نعم ما وقع في بعض نسخ الجامع الصغير خال عن التعليل فكونه غلطاً. من الكتاب صحيح، وما في البحر عن صدر الشريعة قال : إن في المسألة روايتين في رواية تقع رجعية وفي أخرى بائنة وهذا أصح. وبه ظهر أن ما في الهداية هو إحدى الروايتين، فقول من قال إنه غلط أو سهو مما لا ينبغي لأن صدر الشريعة لا يعني أنهما روايتان عن الإمام وإنما أراد بالأولى رواية الجامع الصغير لصدر الإسلام
His saying: (And if she said 'I divorced myself' or 'I chose myself with one divorce,' she becomes irrevocably divorced by one) means in response to his saying 'choose.' And it is valid as a response because divorce is included within the choice; she has performed part of what was delegated to her, just as if he said 'divorce yourself three times' and she divorced once, unlike three without intention. And if she said 'I divorced myself' or 'I chose myself with one divorce, she becomes irrevocably divorced by one' [this is] your matter, and it is different from if she said 'I chose myself' in response to 'divorce yourself' because choice was not delegated to her explicitly or implicitly. And it occurs as ba'in, not raj'i, even though it is explicit, because consideration is given not to her execution but to the husband's delegation. Do you not see that if he ordered her to give a ba'in or raj'i and she reversed it, what the husband ordered takes effect? And Sadr al-Islam mentioned in his Jami' that it occurs as raj'i, considering what the woman executed, according to most books; but in Sharh al-Wiqaya there are two narrations: in one it is raj'i, in another ba'in, and this is more correct. End quote. And thus it appears that what is in al-Hidaya is one of the two narrations. The commentator's saying that it is a mistake and Ibn al-Humam's saying it is an oversight and something that should not be said in such a case, and therefore al-Kafi said that what is in al-Hidaya exists in some copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir, and the correct view is that he does not have the right to take her back (raj'a) as in al-Jami' al-Kabir. End quote. We restricted it to being a response to his saying 'choose' because if he repeated 'choose' three times with a thousand and she said 'I chose myself with one divorce' or 'I chose one divorce,' nothing falls in the case of conjunction because 'one divorce' suffices for a single unit and not three, and the occurrence of one is prevented to avoid harm to him, and one ba'in divorce occurs in the case without conjunction by agreement. And no wealth is due if she meant the first or second divorce; but if she meant the third, all the thousand is due because the wealth is specific to the third. So it is in Sharh al-Talkhis, and it is a commentary on what we have presented. And from it in al-Muhit: If he said 'choose' and she said 'I did,' it does not fall because this is a metaphor for her saying 'I chose' and by it nothing falls, so this is similar. And if he said 'choose yourself' and she said 'I did,' it falls for what we have explained. End quote. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If he said 'I sold your affair to you for a thousand' and she chose herself in the session, she becomes irrevocably divorced and the wealth is due. End quote. His saying: (Your affair is in your hand in one divorce or choose one divorce, and she chose herself, she is divorced revocably) because he gave her choice in one divorce, and it is subject to the possibility of return, and restricting irrevocability, when it is associated with the explicit, becomes revocable. His saying: (And Sadr al-Islam mentioned, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: And what occurred in al-Hidaya that he has the right of return (raj'a), the commentators said it is a mistake of the book, and the correct narration is that it is one and he does not have the right of return because the narrations of al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and most copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir are like this, except for al-Jami' al-Saghir of Sadr al-Islam, for he mentioned in it something like what is mentioned in the book; so it is in al-'Inaya. And I say: How can what is in al-Hidaya be a mistake of the book when he has explained the matter by saying that this wording necessitates separation after the expiry of the waiting period, as if she chose herself after the waiting period? So the correct view, as in the commentary, is to declare it a mistake. Yes, what occurred in some copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir without explanation, so it being a mistake from the book is correct. And what is in al-Bahr from Sadr al-Shari'a said: There are two narrations in the matter, in one it is raj'i, in another ba'in, and this is more correct. And thus it appears that what is in al-Hidaya is one of the two narrations. So the statement of those who said it is a mistake or an oversight is not proper, because Sadr al-Shari'a does not mean that they are two narrations from the Imam, but rather by the first he meant the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir of Sadr al-Islam.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the nature of the divorce (ba'in vs. raj'i) when a wife responds to the husband's delegation (tafwid) by saying 'I divorced myself' or 'I chose myself with one divorce.' The author explains that such a response is valid because divorce is included within the delegated option. The divorce that occurs is ba'in (irrevocable), not raj'i (revocable), because the husband's delegation is controlling. If he ordered a specific type and she did the opposite, his order prevails. However, Sadr al-Islam in his Jami' opined that it is raj'i, considering the wife's execution. But Sharh al-Wiqaya states there are two narrations: one saying raj'i, another ba'in, and the latter is more correct (asahh). The author then discusses the confusion in al-Hidaya, which reportedly states that the husband has the right to take her back (raj'a). Commentators like Ibn al-Humam consider this a mistake. The dispute is resolved by noting that there are two narrations: one from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Sadr al-Islam (raj'i) and the more common view from al-Jami' al-Kabir (ba'in). The stronger position is that it is ba'in and the husband does not own the raj'a. The passage also covers secondary issues: if the husband repeats 'choose' three times with a thousand, and the wife chooses one divorce without specifying, nothing falls if it is with conjunction (due to harm to husband), but one ba'in falls without conjunction by agreement. Wealth is due only if she meant the third divorce. The author concludes with a short matn: if the husband says 'your affair is in your hand in one divorce' or 'choose one divorce' and she chooses herself, the divorce is raj'i because the delegation is limited to one divorce, which is naturally revocable.

Key Terms
بائن (ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that dissolves the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage contract.
رجعي (raj'i): A revocable divorce; the husband can take the wife back during the waiting period without a new contract.
تفويض الطلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Delegation of the power to divorce to the wife; the husband gives her the choice to divorce herself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the mufta bihi (relied upon) position regarding the wife's response 'طلقت نفسي' to 'اختاري'?
A) It is raj'i.
B) It is ba'in.
C) It is invalid.
D) It is a false divorce.

Key Takeaway
The stronger Hanafi view is that the wife's self-divorce in tafwid results in a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, not raj'i.

The Requirement to Mention the Self in Al-Amr bi al-Yad
Explaining the conditions for the wife's valid response when given the right to divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of mentioning the self in the wife's response in al-amr bi al-yad and apply it to determine the validity of different expressions.

Core Idea
In al-amr bi al-yad, if the wife does not say 'myself', no divorce occurs—explicit mention is mandatory.

In the Hanafi school, when a husband gives his wife the authority to divorce herself by saying 'Amruki bi yadiki' or 'Ikhtari', the wife's response must explicitly mention herself. This lesson examines the evidence for this condition and explores which expressions are acceptable and which are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
Recognize that the passage begins by stating that the wife must mention herself (nafs) or its equivalent in her response.
This is the key legal condition: without explicit mention of the self, the divorce does not occur.
2
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The requirement is derived from the parallel with takhyir. In takhyir, if the husband says 'Ikhtari', the wife must say 'Ikhtartu nafsi' for divorce to occur. Similarly, in al-amr bi al-yad, she must explicitly reference herself.
The evidence is qiyas, which classifies the dalil as zanni in thubut and dalala.
3
Distinguish between takhyir and al-amr bi al-yad
The passage notes that the view in Al-Bada'i' comparing the two is weak; the commentary in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq favors explicit mention.
Understand the intra-madhhab difference: the text rejects the analogy that would allow less explicit responses.
4
Apply the principle of suitable expressions
The passage lists expressions that are valid from the wife: 'Taliqtu nafsi', 'Anti haram', 'Ana bain', etc., and invalid ones like 'Anta taliq'.
Apply the rule that only expressions that can effect divorce from the husband work from the wife, except 'ikhtiyar' which is a special case.
5
Evaluate the husband's intention regarding number
If the husband does not intend a specific number, one irrevocable divorce (ba'in) occurs. The passage discusses a case from Al-Khaniyyah.
This is a separate sub-rule that interacts with the condition of mentioning the self.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق فصل في الأمر باليد اختاري لا بد من ذكر النفس أو ما يقوم مقامها للدليل الدال على اشتراطه في الاختيار. وفي المحيط : لو جعل أمرها بيدها فقالت طلقت ولم تقل نفسي لا يقع كما في الخيار لو قالت اخترت لا يقع، ولو قالت عنيت نفسي إن كانت في المجلس تصدق لأنها تملك الإنشاء وإلا فلا اهـ. وهو صريح في مخالفة ما في البدائع الأمر باليد كالتخيير إلى شيئين فدل على ضعفه. وقيد بنية الثلاث لأنه لو لم ينو عدداً أو نوى واحدة أو ثنتين في الحرة وقعت واحدة بائنة، وقدمنا أنه لا بد من نية التفويض إليها ديانة أو يدل الحال عليه قضاء. وفي الخانية : امرأة قالت لزوجها في الخصومة إن كان ما في يدك في يدي استنقذت نفسي فقال الزوج الذي في يدي في يدك فقالت المرأة طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً فقال لها الزوج قولي مرة أخرى فقالت المرأة نفسي ثلاثاً فقال الزوج لم أنو الطلاق بقولي الذي في يدي في يدك فإنها تطلق ثلاثاً بقولها ثانياً طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً حتى لو لم يقل لها قولي مرة أخرى كان القول قوله قضاء وديانة. وفي فتح القدير : وإذا علم أن الأمر باليد مما يراد به الثلاث فإذا قال الزوج نويت التفويض في واحدة بعدما طلقت نفسها ثلاثاً في الجواب يحلف أنه ما أراد الثلاث اهـ. وقيد بقولها اخترت نفسي لأنها لو قالت في جوابه أمري بيدي لا يصح قياساً واستحساناً كما قدمنا. وفي الخلاصة : لو قالت في جوابه ملكت نفسي أمري كان باطلاً ولو قالت اخترت أمري كان جائزاً .اهـ. فالأصل إن كل لفظ يصلح للإيقاع من الزوج يصلح جواباً من المرأة وما لا فلا إلا لفظ الاختيار خاصة فإنه ليس من ألفاظ الطلاق ويصلح جواباً منها. كذا في البدائع. ولذا قال في الاختيار وغيره: لو قال لها أمرك بيدك فقالت أنت علي حرام أو أنت مني بائن أو أنا منك بائن فهو جواب لأن هذه الألفاظ تفيد الطلاق كما إذا قالت طلقت نفسي، ولو قالت أنت طالق لم يقع شيء، ولو قالت أنا منك طالق أو أنا طالق وقع لأن المرأة توصف بالطلاق دون الرجل .اهـ.
Book of Divorce, Chapter on the Command by Hand. 'Choose': It is necessary to mention the self or what stands in its place due to the evidence indicating its requirement in choice. In Al-Muhit: If he placed her command in her hand and she said 'I divorced' and did not say 'myself', it does not occur, just as in the option if she said 'I chose' it does not occur. And if she said 'I meant myself', if she was in the session she is believed because she owns the initiation, otherwise not. End quote. It is explicit in contradicting what is in Al-Bada'i': 'The command by hand is like giving choice to two things', so it indicates its weakness. And it is restricted by the intention of three because if he did not intend a number or intended one or two for a free woman, one irrevocable divorce occurs, and we have stated that the intention of delegation to her is necessary religiously or the situation indicates it judicially. In Al-Khaniyyah: A woman said to her husband in litigation 'If what is in your hand is in my hand, I rescue myself', and the husband said 'What is in my hand is in your hand', and the woman said 'I divorced myself three times', and the husband said 'Say again', and the woman said 'myself three times', then the husband said 'I did not intend divorce by saying what is in my hand is in your hand', then she is divorced three times by her second statement 'I divorced myself three times', such that if he did not say 'Say again', his word is accepted judicially and religiously. And in Fath al-Qadir: And if it is known that the command by hand is intended for three, then if the husband says 'I intended delegation in one' after she divorced herself three times in response, he is made to swear that he did not intend three. End quote. And it is restricted by her saying 'I chose myself' because if she said in response 'My command is in my hand', it is not valid by analogy and istihsan as we have stated. In Al-Khulasa: If she said in response 'I owned myself, my command', it is void; and if she said 'I chose my command', it is valid. End quote. So the principle is that every expression that is suitable for effecting divorce from the husband is suitable as a response from the woman, and what is not, is not, except the expression 'choice' specifically, for it is not from the expressions of divorce but is suitable as a response from her. Thus in Al-Bada'i'. And therefore it is said in Al-Ikhtiyar and others: If he said to her 'Your command is in your hand' and she said 'You are forbidden to me' or 'You are irrevocably separated from me' or 'I am irrevocably separated from you', it is a response because these expressions indicate divorce, just as if she said 'I divorced myself'. And if she said 'You are divorced', nothing occurs; and if she said 'I am divorced from you' or 'I am divorced', it occurs because the woman is described by divorce, not the man. End quote.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the chapter on al-amr bi al-yad (command by hand) where a husband gives his wife the authority to divorce herself. The passage opens by stating the condition that when the husband says 'Ikhtari' (choose), the wife must mention herself (nafs) or something equivalent in her response, such as 'I choose myself'. Evidence for this requirement is referenced. The commentary then contrasts al-amr bi al-yad with takhyir (choice), noting that in al-amr bi al-yad, if the wife says 'I divorced' without 'myself', it does not occur, whereas in takhyir, if she says 'I chose' without 'myself', it also does not occur. However, if she meant herself and is still in the session, she is believed because she owns the initiation. This differs from Al-Bada'i' which compares al-amr bi al-yad to takhyir, but the author here indicates that view is weak. Next, the passage discusses the effect of the husband's intention regarding the number of divorces: if he intends a specific number, that number takes effect; otherwise, one irrevocable divorce (ba'in) occurs. A case from Al-Khaniyyah illustrates how the wife's repeated statements and the husband's intention interact. The passage then shifts to the principle (asl) that any expression that can effect divorce from the husband (e.g., 'You are divorced') can also serve as the wife's valid response, except the word 'choice' (ikhtiyar), which is not a divorce expression but still valid from the wife. Examples include 'You are forbidden to me' (anti haram) and 'I am irrevocably separated from you' (ana mink ba'in). However, if she says 'You are divorced' (anta taliq), it does not occur because the woman is described by divorce, not the man. The passage also notes that if she says 'I am divorced' (ana taliq) or 'I am divorced from you', it does occur.

Key Terms
الأمر باليد (al-amr bi al-yad): The husband giving his wife the authority to divorce herself by saying 'Amruki bi yadiki' (your command is in your hand).
نفس (nafs): The wife's self; must be mentioned in her response for the divorce to be valid.
اختيار (ikhtiyar): The act of choosing; when the husband says 'Ikhtari' it is a form of delegation, and the wife's response must mention herself.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage and does not allow revocation without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The divorce occurs because 'taliqtu' implies herself.
B) The divorce does not occur because she did not mention herself.
C) It is valid if she intended herself even without saying it.
D) It is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
The wife's response in al-amr bi al-yad must explicitly mention herself or an equivalent; otherwise, no divorce occurs.

Talaq — Divorce
